Compensating Transformed Property: The Dispute on Tanned Skin
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for destroyed tanned skin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding compensation for destroyed tanned skin, and explain why the author considers the dispute to have no practical consequence.

Core Idea
When a usurper destroys tanned skin, Imam Abu Hanifa says no compensation; the Sahibayn say yes — but the net result is the same.

The passage examines a nuanced case from the law of usurpation: when the usurper transforms an item (tans a skin) and then destroys it before returning it. The two main authorities within the Hanafi school disagree on whether compensation is due. However, as the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq points out, the practical outcome is identical, raising a question about the purpose of such ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The usurper transforms the skin by tanning, making it more valuable. He then destroys it (itlaf) before returning it. Who gets what in compensation?
The vinegar case is similar but less disputed.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam holds that the usurper compensates only the vinegar, not the tanned skin. The value added by tanning is the result of the usurper's own effort and materials; the owner's right is limited to the original skin's value.
Dalil: The increase is due to the usurper's act, so no liability for that increase.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the usurper compensates the full value of the tanned skin, but the owner must return the tanning cost (increase from tanning). Ownership of the skin persists after tanning.
Dalil: The owner can take back the tanned skin upon compensation, so destroying it is like destroying any owned property.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The author notes that subtracting the tanning cost from the tanned value gives the untanned value. Thus, the net compensation is the same. The dispute is nominal, not practical.
This is a key insight: differences in legal reasoning may not affect the final ruling.
5
Apply to other transformation cases
The passage extends the principle: making a fur, bag, or vessel from the skin, or turning wine into vinegar. Similar logic applies: the usurper may own the transformed item but compensates the original value.
Other examples: clay into pot, basin by weight. Owner may have option to take item or claim compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن أتلفهما ضمن الخل فقط) يعني لو أتلف الغاصب الخل والجلد المدبوغ في يده قبل أن يردهما إلى صاحبهما ضمن الخل ولا يضمن الجلد المدبوغ، وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : يضمن قيمة الجلد مدبوغاً أيضاً ويعطي ما زاد الدباغ فيه لأن ملكه باق فيه ولهذا يأخذه وهو مال متقوم فيضمنه له مدبوغاً بالاستهلاك. وللإمام أن ماليته وتقويمه حصل بفعل الغاصب وفعله متقوم لاستعماله مالاً متقوماً فيه، ولذا كان له حبسة والجلد تبع للملك وملكه باقٍ فيه . ثم قيل : يضمن قيمة جلد مدبوغ ويعطي ما زاد الدباغ. قال فخر الإسلام وغيره في شرح الجامع الصغير : قولهما «يعطي ما زاد الدباغ فيه محمول على ما إذا قوم الجلد بالدراهم والدباغ بالدنانير، أما إذا قومهما بالدراهم أو بالدنانير فيطرح عنه ذلك القدر ويؤخذ منه الباقي وهو قيمة جلد مذكى غير مدبوغ. وفي الكافي : وإن استهلكه يضمن قيمته طاهراً غير مدبوغ والجمهور على أنه يضمن قيمته مدبوغاً. ولو جعل الجلد فرواً أو جراباً أو زقاً لم يكن للمغصوب منه عليه سبيل، وإن خللها بصب الخل فيها قيل يكون للغاصب بغير شيء عند أبي حنيفة، سواء صارت خلاً من ساعتها أو بمرور الزمان عليها لأن خلط الخل استهلاك واستهلاك الخمر لا الضمان وعندهما إن صارت خلاً من ساعتها فكما قال أبو حنيفة أنه استهلاك، وإن صارت بمرور الزمان كان الخل بينهما على قدر حقوقهما كيلاً. وفي التتارخانية: وإذا غصب تراباً أو لبنة أو جعله ،آنية فإن كان له قيمة فهو مثل الحنطة إذا طحن، فإن لم يكن له قيمة فلا شيء عليه من الضمان وفي القدوري : المغصوب منه يكون أسوة للغرماء في الثمن ولا يكون أخص بشيء من ذلك. وفي الذخيرة اتخذ كوزاً من طين غيره كان الكوز له، فإن قال رب الطين أنا أمرته به فهو أحق به وفي نوادر ابن سماعة: رجل طشتاً لغيره وهو مما يباع وزناً فربه بالخيار إن شاء أمسك الطشت ولا شيء له، وإن شاء دفعه وأخذ قيمته وكذا كل مصنوع قيد بقوله «أتلفهما لأنهما لو هلكا لا يضمن بالإجماع والمجمع عليه لا يحتاج إلى دليل لأن دليله الإجماع ولم يظهر لهذا الاختلاف في التقويم فائدة عندي فإن قيمة جلد مدبوغ بعد أن يطرح عنه قدر ما زاد الدباغ فيه جلد ذكي غير مدبوغ بعينها، وقولهم لم ينظر إلى قيمته ذكياً غير مذبوح بعينها وإلى قيمته مذبوحاً فيضمن فضل ما بينهما صريح في ذلك، فما فائدة الاختلاف والمآل واحد؟ ولهذا لو دبغه بما لا قيمة لا له يضمنه بالاستهلاك وفي السغناقي ومن أتلف الشاة المذبوحة المتروكة التسمية عمداً لا اهـ . يضمن هشم . هي قيمة
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he destroys both, he compensates only the vinegar). Meaning if the usurper destroys the vinegar and the tanned skin while in his hand before returning them to their owner, he compensates the vinegar and does not compensate the tanned skin. This is the saying of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Sahibayn) said: He compensates the value of the tanned skin as well and gives the increase from tanning, because his ownership remains in it and therefore he takes it, and it is valuable property so he compensates it for him tanned upon consumption. And for Imam: its value and valuation occurred by the act of the usurper, and his act is valuable because he used valuable property in it, and therefore he had the right to detain it, and the skin is subsidiary to ownership and his ownership remains in it. Then it was said: He compensates the value of tanned skin and gives the increase from tanning. Fakhr al-Islam and others said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Their saying 'he gives the increase from tanning' is understood when the skin is valued in dirhams and the tanning in dinars, but if both are valued in dirhams or both in dinars, that amount is subtracted and the remainder is taken, which is the value of a skinned slaughtered animal not tanned. In al-Kafi: And if he consumes it, he compensates its value as pure (i.e., after tanning) but not tanned, and the majority (jumhur) hold he compensates its value tanned. And if he makes the skin into a fur, bag, or waterskin, the usurped-from has no recourse against it. And if he makes it vinegar by pouring vinegar into it, it is said that it becomes the usurper's for nothing according to Abu Hanifa, whether it becomes vinegar instantly or over time, because mixing vinegar is consumption and consumption of wine does not require compensation. According to the two (Sahibayn), if it becomes vinegar instantly, it is as Abu Hanifa said that it is consumption, and if it becomes over time, the vinegar is between them according to their respective rights by measure. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: And if he usurps dirt or a brick and makes it a vessel, if it has value then it is like wheat when ground, and if it has no value then no compensation upon him. In al-Quduri: The usurped-from becomes an equal among creditors in the price and does not have a specific claim on anything from that. In al-Dhakhira: If he makes a cup from another's clay, the cup is his, and if the owner of the clay says 'I ordered him to do it', then he has more right to it. In Nawadir Ibn Sami'a: A man had a basin belonging to another, which is sold by weight, so its owner has the option: if he wishes he may keep the basin and nothing is owed, and if he wishes he may hand it over and take its value. Likewise every manufactured item. He restricted with his saying 'if he destroys both' because if they perish by natural causes, he does not compensate by consensus, and what is agreed upon does not need proof because its proof is consensus. And it appears to me that this difference in valuation has no benefit, because the value of tanned skin after subtracting the amount of increase from tanning is exactly the value of an untanned slaughtered skin. And their statement that he does not look at its value as an unskinned slaughtered animal but at its value skinned and then compensates the difference between them is explicit in that. So what is the benefit of the difference when the outcome is one? And therefore if he tans with something of no value, he compensates it upon consumption. And in al-Sighnaqi: And whoever intentionally destroys a slaughtered sheep on which the tasmiya was omitted, he guarantees... he smashes... it is value.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling when the usurper destroys the transformed items (vinegar and tanned skin) before returning them to the owner. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the usurper only compensates for the vinegar, not the tanned skin. The justification is that the value of the tanned skin was created by the usurper's own act (tanning), and since he used valuable materials, his act is itself valuable. However, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the usurper must compensate the full value of the tanned skin as well, but then the usurper receives back the increase (the cost of tanning) from the owner? Actually, the text says: 'yadman qeemat al-jild madbughan aydan wa yu'ti ma zad al-dibagh fihi' – he compensates the value of the tanned skin and gives the increase from tanning. This means he pays the full tanned value, then the owner returns the tanning cost to him. So the net effect is the same as the Imam's view? The commentary by Fakhr al-Islam explains that if both are valued in the same currency, the result is the same as the value of an untanned skin. The author (possibly Ibn al-Humam or the commentator) then remarks that the dispute seems pointless because the net compensation is identical. The passage also discusses other cases: if the skin is made into a fur, bag, etc., the owner cannot reclaim it because the transformation is too drastic; the usurper becomes owner and compensates the original value. Similarly, if vinegar is made by adding vinegar, there is a dispute. The text then digresses to examples of usurping dirt and making pottery, and the owner's option to take the manufactured item or claim compensation. The common thread is that when the usurper transforms the item using his own labor or materials, the owner may have an option. The passage ends with a note that if the items perish without human action (halka), there is consensus that the usurper does not compensate, which is why the matn specified destruction (itlaf).

Key Terms
إتلاف (itlaf): Destruction or consumption of property by the usurper. In this context, it triggers liability for compensation.
استهلاك (istihlak): Consumption of property, such as eating or using up. In this passage, mixing vinegar into wine is considered consumption of the wine, which does not incur liability because wine is not valuable property for Muslims.
دباغ (dibagh): Tanning; the process of treating animal skin to make it durable. In the passage, the increase in value due to tanning is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the usurper destroys both the vinegar and the tanned skin before returning them, what does he compensate?
A) The vinegar and the tanned skin (with deduction for tanning cost).
B) Only the vinegar.
C) Only the tanned skin.
D) Nothing, because the items were transformed.

Key Takeaway
The dispute on compensating tanned skin is nominal because the net compensation is identical in both views.

Liability for Sinful Objects: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for destroying objects of sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability for destroying objects prepared for sin, and apply the tarjih based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Objects prepared for sin may lose legal value, and the religious duty to destroy them can override liability.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person breaks a musical instrument or spills wine belonging to another, is he liable for compensation? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, but the Sahibayn argue that such objects have no legal value (taqawwum) because they are prepared for sin, and the Shari'ah itself commands their destruction. Understanding this difference is crucial for applying the correct ruling in matters of tort and property.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Positions
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the person is liable (daman), while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no liability exists.
This is a clear intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Follow the Opponent's Proof (Sahibayn)
Examine the reasoning of the Sahibayn: they argue that musical instruments (mi'zaf) are prepared for sin, so they lose their legal value (taqawwum), analogous to wine (khamr) which has no value for Muslims. Additionally, the act of destruction is permitted—even commanded—by the Lawgiver, citing the hadith: 'I was sent to break the flutes and kill the pigs.' Thus, the destroyer is acting righteously and should not be liable.
The hadith is a key dalil naqli.
3
Analyse the Hanafi Response (Imam)
Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that property rights persist despite sinful use; the owner still has a right to compensation unless the property is formally confiscated by the authorities. Destruction without due process remains a tort.
Imam's view treats the objects as still being mal.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: under Imam's view, the destroyer must pay compensation; under Sahibayn, no compensation is due.
This affects real cases of such destruction.
5
Identify the Tarjih
Later Hanafi fatwa practice often follows the Sahibayn due to the explicit hadith. The text itself does not give a definitive tarjih, but the hadith provides strong support.
The authority of the hadith outweighs the general principle of property protection here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (ومن كسر معزفاً أو أراق سكراً أو منصفاً ضمن) وهذا قول الإمام . وقالا : لا يضمنها لأنها معدة للمعصية فيسقط تقومها كالخمر ولأنه فعله بإذن الشارع لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام بعثت لكسر المزامير وقتل الخنازير ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا البحر الرائق ج ١٥/٨
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And whoever breaks a musical instrument (mi'zaf) or spills wine (sukr) or a vessel (munsaf) guarantees [i.e., is liable]. This is the saying of Imam. And the two (Sahibayn) said: He does not guarantee them because they are prepared for sin, so their valuation falls like wine, and because his action is with the permission of the Lawgiver due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'I was sent to break the flutes (mazamir) and kill the pigs', and due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'when...' [incomplete].
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability of a person who destroys objects that are inherently associated with sin: musical instruments (mi'zaf) and wine (sukr). The matn states that one who breaks such items is liable (daman). However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the person is liable for compensation, treating these as valuable property despite their sinful use. The two (Sahibayn) disagree, arguing that such objects have no legal value (taqawwum) because they are prepared for sin, analogous to wine (khamr) which has no value for Muslims. Additionally, they argue that the act of destroying these items is actually commanded by the Shari'ah, citing the Prophet's hadith: 'I was sent to break the flutes and kill the pigs.' This implies that the destruction is a virtuous act, not a tort. Therefore, no compensation is due. The text ends abruptly with an incomplete hadith reference. The dispute hinges on whether the objects retain any residual value despite their prohibited use. Imam's view considers that the owner's property rights are not completely nullified, so destruction requires compensation. The Sahibayn's view prioritizes the religious obligation to destroy such items, overriding property rights. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school often follows Sahibayn in this case, as the hadith provides a clear proof.

Key Terms
معزف (mi'zaf): A musical instrument. In this context, it is considered an object prepared for sin (ma'dah li'l-ma'siyah).
سكر (sukr): Intoxicating beverage, specifically wine or any intoxicant. In the text, it is used interchangeably with khamr.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Valuable property that commands compensation. Sahibayn argue that these objects are not mutaqawwim because they are prepared for sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is a person not liable for breaking a musical instrument belonging to another?
A) Because the instrument was not valuable.
B) Because the instrument was prepared for sin and thus has no legal value, and the act is permitted by the Shari'ah.
C) Because the owner has no right to compensation for sin-related items.
D) Because the instrument was already broken.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, objects exclusively prepared for sin may lose their legal value, and the religious duty to destroy them can remove liability for compensation, following the Sahibayn's view based on the hadith.

Liability for Tanning Usurped Hide: Imam vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for tanned usurped hide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability for a tanned usurped hide and apply the ruling to similar manufacturing cases.

Core Idea
A usurper's work on stolen property does not transfer ownership of the increased value.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a usurper tans a stolen hide and then destroys it, what must he compensate? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that compensation is only for the original hide value, while the two companions (Sahibayn) argue for the tanned value minus the cost of tanning. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to mixing labor with misappropriated property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is tanning (dabgh) a usurped hide, followed by destruction (istihlak) of both hide and tanning material (vinegar). The dispute is about the measure of compensation: original value vs. enhanced value.
This is a ghasp (usurpation) case, not a sale or hire.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Imam Abu Hanifa: liable only for value of untanned hide (value of a slaughtered hide). Reasoning: the increase in value is due to the usurper's own work and expenditure; the owner's ownership remains, but the usurper has the right to detain the hide until his costs are reimbursed.
Qiyas with grinding wheat: the owner gets flour if he pays the grinding fee.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: liable for value of tanned hide, but the usurper gets the cost of tanning. Reasoning: the owner's ownership persists in the hide itself, and the tanned hide is valuable property; destroying it triggers liability for its current value.
The net amount owed may be similar after accounting for tanning costs.
4
Analyze the practical outcome and further scenarios
The commentary notes that if both hide and tanning are valued in the same currency, the net compensation is the value of an untanned hide. Additional scenarios: if the usurper turns the hide into fur, bag, or waterskin, the owner has no recourse; if vinegar is added to wine, the ruling depends on instantaneous vs. gradual change.
The expansion probe explores boundary cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
According to al-Kafi, the majority hold the Sahibayn's view. Thus the relied-upon position is that the usurper owes the tanned value minus the cost of tanning.
This is important for fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدباغ فيه وإن أتلفهما ضمن الخل فقط ولا يضمن الجلد المدبوغ، وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : يضمن قيمة الجلد مدبوغاً أيضاً ويعطي ما زاد الدباغ فيه لأن ملكه باق فيه ولهذا يأخذه وهو مال متقوم فيضمنه له مدبوغاً بالاستهلاك. وللإمام أن ماليته وتقويمه حصل بفعل الغاصب وفعله متقوم لاستعماله مالاً متقوماً فيه، ولذا كان له حبسة والجلد تبع للملك وملكه باقٍ فيه . ثم قيل : يضمن قيمة جلد مدبوغ ويعطي ما زاد الدباغ. قال فخر الإسلام وغيره في شرح الجامع الصغير : قولهما «يعطي ما زاد الدباغ فيه محمول على ما إذا قوم الجلد بالدراهم والدباغ بالدنانير، أما إذا قومهما بالدراهم أو بالدنانير فيطرح عنه ذلك القدر ويؤخذ منه الباقي وهو قيمة جلد مذكى غير مدبوغ. وفي الكافي : وإن استهلكه يضمن قيمته طاهراً غير مدبوغ والجمهور على أنه يضمن قيمته مدبوغاً. ولو جعل الجلد فرواً أو جراباً أو زقاً لم يكن للمغصوب منه عليه سبيل، وإن خللها بصب الخل فيها قيل يكون للغاصب بغير شيء عند أبي حنيفة، سواء صارت خلاً من ساعتها أو بمرور الزمان عليها لأن خلط الخل استهلاك واستهلاك الخمر لا الضمان وعندهما إن صارت خلاً من ساعتها فكما قال أبو حنيفة أنه استهلاك، وإن صارت بمرور الزمان كان الخل بينهما على قدر حقوقهما كيلاً.
Regarding tanning [the hide]: if he destroys both [the hide and the vinegar], he is liable only for the vinegar and is not liable for the tanned hide. This is the statement of Imam [Abu Hanifa]. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: He is liable for the value of the tanned hide as well and gives [the owner] the increase from the tanning because his ownership remains in it, and for this reason he takes it, and it is valuable property, so he is liable for it tanned by destruction. For the Imam: its value and worth came about by the usurper's action, and his action is valuable because he used valuable property in it, so he has the right to detain it, and the hide is subsidiary to ownership, and the owner's ownership remains in it. Then it was said: He is liable for the value of a tanned hide and gives the increase from the tanning. Fakhr al-Islam and others said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Their statement 'he gives the increase from the tanning' is interpreted as when the hide is valued in dirhams and the tanning in dinars. However, if both are valued in dirhams or both in dinars, that amount is deducted and the remainder is taken, which is the value of a slaughtered untanned hide. In al-Kafi: If he consumes it, he is liable for its value as a pure untanned hide, and the majority hold that he is liable for its value tanned. If he made the hide into fur, a bag, or a waterskin, the owner has no claim upon him. If he turned [wine into vinegar] by pouring vinegar into it, it is said that it belongs to the usurper without compensation according to Abu Hanifa, whether it becomes vinegar instantly or over time, because mixing vinegar is consumption and consuming wine does not incur liability. According to the two, if it becomes vinegar instantly, it is as Abu Hanifa said: it is consumption. If it becomes vinegar over time, the vinegar is between them in proportion to their rights by measure.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a usurper who tans a usurped hide. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, specifically between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The core issue is whether the usurper must compensate the owner for the increase in value due to tanning. According to Abu Hanifa, the usurper is only liable for the original value of the hide (as an untanned slaughtered hide) because the increased value is a result of his own work and expenditure, and he has the right to detain the tanned hide until his costs are reimbursed. The two companions argue that since the owner's ownership persists, the usurper is liable for the full tanned value but must be compensated for the cost of tanning. The text then explains that the practical difference may be negligible because the net amount owed is the same. Additional scenarios are discussed: if the usurper turns the hide into other objects like fur or bags, the owner has no claim; if wine turns into vinegar by adding vinegar, the ruling depends on timing and the view of the imams.

Key Terms
الدباغ (al-dabbagh): Tanning; the process of treating animal hide to make it usable.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value; compensation in lieu of the property.
استهلاك (istihlak): Consumption; destruction of the property so that it no longer exists in its original form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (ra), what is the usurper liable for when he tans and destroys a usurped hide?
A) The value of the tanned hide plus the cost of tanning
B) The value of an untanned hide only
C) The value of the tanned hide minus the cost of tanning
D) Nothing because tanning is a beneficial act

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that a usurper who tans and destroys a stole hide owes the tanned value minus his costs, balancing ownership rights and labour compensation.

Usurping an Umm Walad: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Liability
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guarantee of umm walad value in ghasp

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for an umm walad in ghasp and distinguish the Sahibayn's opposing view, explaining the practical consequence.

Core Idea
The umm walad's unique status removes her from valuable property; no guarantee due upon usurpation.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a usurper must pay compensation if an umm walad dies in his possession. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples diverge on the fundamental nature of the umm walad as valuable property. Understanding this dispute reveals how foundational principles of property classification (māl mutaqawwim) shape practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling according to Imam
The author states the ruling: if someone usurps an umm walad or mudabbirah and she dies, he guarantees the mudabbirah but not the umm walad. This is Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn disagree: they hold that the umm walad is also guaranteed because she is valuable property, akin to a mudabbirah.
Sahibayn = Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The dispute hinges on whether the umm walad is māl mutaqawwim. Abu Hanifa says no; Sahibayn say yes, by analogy to mudabbirah.
Māl mutaqawwim = property that can be sold and guaranteed.
4
Connect to earlier rulings
The author links this to the Book of 'Itq, where Abu Hanifa already ruled that the umm walad has no value. The repetition here precludes any misunderstanding that the ghasp ruling might differ.
The objection that repetition is useless is refuted by contextual consistency.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
If the umm walad dies while usurped, under Abu Hanifa the usurper pays nothing; under Sahibayn, he pays her market value.
This practical difference is crucial for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالا : لا يجوز بيع هذه الأشياء لأنها ليست بمال متقوم وجواز البيع ووجوب الضمان مبنيان على المالية. قال رحمه الله: (ومن غصب أم ولد أو مدبرة فمات ضمن قيمة المدبرة لا أم الولد وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : يضمن أم الولد أيضاً لأنها متقومة عندهما كالمدبرة وقد ذكرناه والدليل من الجانبين في كتاب العتق لا يقال قد علم ما ذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى في كتاب العتق أن أم الولد لا قيمة لها عند الإمام حيث قال : وما لام ولد تقوم فذكر أم الولد هنا لا فائدة له لأنا نقول : بل فيه فائدة لأنه ثمة بين الحكم فيما إذا أعتقها الشريك فربما يتوهم شخص أن الحكم في الغصب يخالف ما تقدم فبين المؤلف رحمه الله أنه لا يخالف والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible to sell these things because they are not valuable property, and the permissibility of sale and obligation of guarantee are based on being property. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Whoever usurps an umm walad or a mudabbirah and she dies, he guarantees the value of the mudabbirah but not the umm walad. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two said: He guarantees the umm walad as well because, according to them, she is valuable property like the mudabbirah.' And we have mentioned this, and the evidence from both sides is in the Book of 'Itq. It should not be said: It is known from what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in the Book of 'Itq that the umm walad has no value according to Imam, where he said: 'And what an umm walad possesses is evaluated?' So mentioning the umm walad here has no benefit. For we say: Rather there is benefit because there he clarified the ruling when a partner frees her, and perhaps someone might think that the ruling in usurpation contradicts what preceded. So the author (may Allah have mercy on him) clarified that it does not contradict. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability of a usurper (ghāṣib) for the death of an umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master) or a mudabbirah (a slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone usurps an umm walad and she dies, the usurper does not owe her value, because in his view an umm walad is not considered valuable property (māl mutaqawwim) due to her special status as a prospective mother of the master's child. However, the mudabbirah is valuable, so the usurper guarantees her value. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sāḥibayn), hold the opposite: the umm walad is also valuable property, so the usurper must guarantee her value akin to the mudabbirah. The commentator notes that the detailed evidence for both positions is found in the Book of 'Itq (Emancipation). A potential objection is raised: since Abu Hanifa already ruled in the Book of 'Itq that the umm walad has no value, there seems no need to repeat the ruling here. The commentator responds by explaining that the ruling in 'Itq concerned the case where a partner frees the umm walad, and one might mistakenly think that the ruling in ghasp is different. Thus, the author clarifies that it is not different – the umm walad remains without value in both contexts according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has given birth to a child of her master, thereby acquiring a special status that restricts her sale and makes her free upon the master's death.
مدبرة (mudabbirah): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbīr). She remains a slave during the master's life but is valuable property.
مال متقوم (māl mutaqawwim): Property that is legally recognized as having a monetary value and is permissible to trade; in the context of this passage, it determines whether the usurper is liable for value upon destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, does a usurper guarantee the value of an umm walad if she dies?
A) Yes, he must guarantee her value.
B) No, he does not guarantee her value.
C) He guarantees half her value.
D) It depends on whether she was also a mudabbirah.

Key Takeaway
The critical legal distinction between the umm walad and other slaves determines liability; the umm walad’s special status removes her from the category of valuable property.

The Legal Framework of Shuf'ah: Definition, Proof, and Conditions
Introduction to the book of shuf'ah with definition and key elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shuf'ah, identify its proof from the Sunnah, and list its essential conditions.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a forced ownership of property to prevent neighbourly harm — a right rooted in the Sunnah.

This passage opens the Book of Shuf'ah in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, providing a comprehensive introduction. It defines shuf'ah as forced ownership, cites the Prophetic proof, explains its cause (repelling harm), and outlines its conditions. This lesson will parse each element so you can articulate the Hanafi position clearly.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the legal definition
Identify the key components of the definition: forced ownership (tamlik jaban), the spot (buq'ah), and the buyer's price (bima qama alayh). Understand that 'ownership' includes substance and usufructs, but 'spot' excludes usufructs alone.
The definition is from the matn: 'tamlik al-buq'ah jabran ala al-mushtari bima qama alayh'.
2
Understand the cause (sabab)
The cause of shuf'ah is to prevent harm that arises from bad neighbourhood, such as fire, raising walls, or stirring dust. This is a key element in Hanafi reasoning.
Harm prevention (daf' al-darar) is the underlying rationale.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The evidence is a hadith: the Prophet judged by shuf'ah in every undivided partnership and said 'the neighbour is more entitled'. Recognize that this hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and establishes the ruling.
The phrase 'qada' indicates a legal judgement, not mere advice.
4
Identify the condition (shart)
The condition is that the property be real estate ('aqar) owned by exchange (mamluk bi-badal). This excludes state lands held on sharecropping.
The text says 'shartuha kawn al-mahal 'aqaran'.
5
Recognize the ruling (hukm) and description
The ruling is that claiming shuf'ah is permissible (mubah) when its cause exists. Taking by shuf'ah is like a new purchase, so options (like option of sight) apply.
Shuf'ah is a right, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه وتجب للخليط في نفس المبيع وتجب المشتري به الأخذ من مال . وجه مناسبة الشفعة بالغصب تملك الإنسان مال غيره بلا رضاه في كل منهما، والحق تقديمها عليه لكونها مشروعة دونه ولكن توفر الحاجة إلى معرفته لكثرة الأحكام المتعلقة أوجبت تقديمه والكلام فيها من وجوه الأول في معناه لغة، والثاني شرعاً، والثالث في بيان دليلها، والرابع في بيان سببها، والخامس في ركنها، والسادس في شرطها، والسابع في حكمها وصفتها، فهي لغة مأخوذة من الشفع الذي هو ضد الوتر، وشرعاً ما ذكره المؤلف، ودليلها ما روي أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قضى بالشفعة في كل شركة لم تقسم ربعه أو حائطه وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام الجار أحق بشفعة جاره وسببها دفع الضرر الذي ينشأ من سوء المجاورة على الدوام من حيث إيقاد النار وإعلاء الجدار وإثارة الغبار. وركنها هو أو من البائع. وشرطها كون المحل عقاراً علواً كان أو سفلاً مملوكاً ببدل هو وأما حكمها فهو جواز طلب الشفعة عند تحقق سببها. وصفتها أن الأخذ بها بمنزلة شراء مبتدأ حتى يثبت ما يثبت بالشراء نحو الرد بخيار الرؤية والشرط. قال رحمه الله : (هي تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه هذا في الشرع وزاد بعضهم شركة أو جوار. فقوله تمليك جنس شمل تمليك العين والمنافع، وقوله «البقعة» فصل أخرج به تمليك المنافع. وقوله «جبراً» أخرج به البيع فإنه يكون بالرضا، وقوله بما قام عليه» يعني حقيقة أو حكماً كما سيأتي في الخمر وغيره والمراد تمليك البقعة أو بعضها ليشمل ما إذا اشتراها أحد شفعائها ففي التتارخانية : اشترى الجار داراً ولها جار آخر من جانب آخر وطلب الشفعة تقسم الدار بين المشتري والجار نصفين. وفي التتارخانية وإنما تجب في الأراضي التي يملك رقابها حتى لا تجب في الأراضي التي حازها الإمام لبيت المال وتدفع للناس مزارعة فصار لهم فيها بناء وأشجار فإن بيع هذه الأراضي باطل، وإنما تجب بحق الملك في الأراضي حتى لو بيعت دار
Book of Shuf'ah: Ownership of the spot (property) forcibly on the buyer at what he paid, and it is established for the partner in the very sold property, and the buyer is obliged to take from his wealth. The appropriateness of shuf'ah with usurpation is that in both a person owns another's property without his consent, but the right (of shuf'ah) should be presented after it because it is legislated while usurpation is not, but the abundance of related rulings necessitated its priority. The discussion is in seven aspects: first: its linguistic meaning, second: its legal meaning, third: its evidence, fourth: its cause, fifth: its pillar, sixth: its condition, seventh: its ruling and description. Linguistically it is derived from 'shaf' which is the opposite of 'watr' (odd). Legally it is what the author mentioned. Its evidence is what has been reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) adjudicated by shuf'ah in every partnership that had not divided, whether a quarter or a wall, and he said: 'The neighbour is more entitled to his neighbour's shuf'ah.' Its cause is to repel harm that arises from bad neighbourhood permanently, such as kindling fire, raising walls, and stirring dust. Its pillar is he or from the seller. Its condition is that the place be real estate, whether upper or lower, owned by exchange. As for its ruling, it is the permissibility of claiming shuf'ah when its cause is realized. Its description is that taking by it is like a new purchase, so that what is established by purchase is established (like return due to option of sight or condition). The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'It is ownership of the spot forcibly on the buyer at what he paid.' This is in the law, and some added 'partnership or neighbourhood'. So his saying 'ownership' is a genus that includes ownership of the substance and usufructs. His saying 'the spot' specifies and excludes ownership of usufructs. His saying 'forcibly' excludes sale because it is by consent. His saying 'at what he paid' means in reality or legally as will come in wine and other things. The intended meaning is ownership of the spot or part of it, to include the case where one of the pre-emptors buys it. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: A neighbour bought a house and it has another neighbour from another side and he requests shuf'ah, the house is divided between the buyer and the neighbour in halves. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: It is only established in lands whose titles are owned, so it is not established in lands that the imam has taken for the treasury and given to people as sharecropping, so they have buildings and trees in them; the sale of these lands is invalid, and it (shuf'ah) is only established by right of ownership in lands, so even if a house is sold...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Shuf'ah (Pre-emption). It begins with the legal definition: shuf'ah is the forced acquisition of a property (the 'spot') from the buyer at the price he paid. The commentator then explains why this book follows the Book of Ghasp: both involve taking another's property without consent, but shuf'ah is legitimate whereas ghasp is not. However, due to the many rulings of ghasp, it was placed first. The author enumerates seven aspects of the discussion: (1) linguistic meaning, (2) legal meaning, (3) proof, (4) cause, (5) pillar, (6) condition, (7) ruling and description. Linguistically, 'shuf'ah' is derived from 'shaf' (even number), opposite of 'watr' (odd). Legally, it is the definition given in the matn. The proof is a hadith: the Prophet (SAW) judged by shuf'ah in every undivided partnership, and said 'the neighbour is more entitled'. The cause is to prevent harm from bad neighbours. The pillar is ambiguous: 'huwa aw min al-bā'i' – likely meaning the seller or the buyer? The condition: the property must be real estate owned by exchange. The ruling: it is permissible to claim shuf'ah when its cause exists. The description: taking by shuf'ah is like a new purchase, so options apply. Then the commentator parses the matn's definition: 'ownership' includes both substance and usufructs; 'spot' excludes usufructs; 'forcibly' excludes sale; 'at what he paid' includes actual price and legal equivalent. The passage ends with examples from al-Tatarkhaniyya about division of property when a neighbour exercises shuf'ah, and a note that shuf'ah does not apply to state-owned lands given on sharecropping.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Forced ownership of a property on the buyer at the price he paid; a right of pre-emption.
بقعة (buq'ah): The piece of land or property (the 'spot') that is subject to shuf'ah.
خليط (khalīṭ): A partner in the property itself; one who shares ownership in the same sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a property to be subject to shuf'ah?
A) It must be movable property.
B) It must be real estate owned by exchange.
C) It must be a garden with trees.
D) It must be inherited property.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a forced right of ownership to prevent harm from new neighbours, established by hadith, and subject to the condition that the property be real estate owned by exchange.

Definition of Shuf'a: Linguistic and Legal Meaning
Defines shuf'a linguistically and legally with seven aspects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of shuf'a in Hanafi fiqh and identify its key components (cause, pillar, condition, ruling).

Core Idea
Shuf'a is the right to compulsorily purchase real estate from the buyer to prevent harm from bad neighborhood.

The passage begins the Book of Shuf'a by defining it linguistically and legally. Linguistically, shuf'a derives from shaf' (pair) because it joins two shares. Legally, it is the compulsory ownership of a sold plot upon the purchaser for the price paid. This lesson unpacks the definition and its seven aspects, providing a foundation for understanding this unique right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origin
Find the root word 'shaf' and understand its meaning as the opposite of 'witr' (odd). Recognize that shuf'a joins the buyer's share with the pre-emptor's share.
This is a classical entry point for legal definitions.
2
State the legal definition
Quote the author's definition: 'ownership of the plot compulsorily upon the purchaser for what he paid'. Note the key elements: ownership, plot, compulsion, price.
Memorize this definition as the standard Hanafi formulation.
3
Dissect the author's wording
Analyze each component: 'ownership' (genus includes substance and usufructs), 'plot' (excludes usufructs, limits to real estate), 'compulsorily' (excludes voluntary sale), 'for what he paid' (actual price or legally equivalent).
This is a typical commentary exercise (sharh) that clarifies scope.
4
List the seven aspects
The passage outlines: linguistic meaning, legal meaning, proof, cause, pillar, condition, ruling. Note each briefly from the text.
These aspects structure the entire discussion of shuf'a.
5
Identify the cause
The cause is repelling the harm arising from bad neighboring, such as fire, high walls, or dust. This teleological aspect justifies the compulsory nature.
Cause (sabab) is distinct from condition (shart) in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه وتجب للخليط في نفس المبيع وتجب المشتري به الأخذ من مال. وجه مناسبة الشفعة بالغصب تملك الإنسان مال غيره بلا رضاه في كل منهما، والحق تقديمها عليه لكونها مشروعة دونه ولكن توفر الحاجة إلى معرفته لكثرة الأحكام المتعلقة أوجبت تقديمه والكلام فيها من وجوه الأول في معناه لغة، والثاني شرعاً، والثالث في بيان دليلها، والرابع في بيان سببها، والخامس في ركنها، والسادس في شرطها، والسابع في حكمها وصفتها، فهي لغة مأخوذة من الشفع الذي هو ضد الوتر، وشرعاً ما ذكره المؤلف، ودليلها ما روي أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قضى بالشفعة في كل شركة لم تقسم ربعه أو حائطه وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام الجار أحق بشفعة جاره وسببها دفع الضرر الذي ينشأ من سوء المجاورة على الدوام من حيث إيقاد النار وإعلاء الجدار وإثارة الغبار. وركنها هو أو من البائع. وشرطها كون المحل عقاراً علواً كان أو سفلاً مملوكاً ببدل هو وأما حكمها فهو جواز طلب الشفعة عند تحقق سببها. وصفتها أن الأخذ بها بمنزلة شراء مبتدأ حتى يثبت ما يثبت بالشراء نحو الرد بخيار الرؤية والشرط. قال رحمه الله : (هي تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه هذا في الشرع وزاد بعضهم شركة أو جوار. فقوله تمليك جنس شمل تمليك العين والمنافع، وقوله «البقعة» فصل أخرج به تمليك المنافع. وقوله «جبراً» أخرج به البيع فإنه يكون بالرضا، وقوله بما قام عليه» يعني حقيقة أو حكماً كما سيأتي في الخمر وغيره والمراد تمليك البقعة أو بعضها ليشمل ما إذا اشتراها أحد شفعائها ففي التتارخانية : اشترى الجار داراً ولها جار آخر من جانب آخر وطلب الشفعة تقسم الدار بين المشتري والجار نصفين. وفي التتارخانية وإنما تجب في الأراضي التي يملك رقابها حتى لا تجب في الأراضي التي حازها الإمام لبيت المال وتدفع للناس مزارعة فصار لهم فيها بناء وأشجار فإن بيع هذه الأراضي باطل، وإنما تجب بحق الملك في الأراضي حتى لو بيعت دار للخليط في نفس المبيع ثم في حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق إن كان خاصاً ثم للجار بجنبها دار الوقف فلا شفعة للوقف ولا يأخذها المتولي قال ابن قاضي زاده : إذا كان حقيقة الشفعة التمليك لزم أن لا يكون لقوله الشفعة تثبت بعقد البيع وتستقر بالإشهاد صحة إذ الثبوت لا يتصور بدون التحقق وحين عقد البيع والإشهاد لم يوجد الأخذ بالتراضي ولا بقضاء القاضي ولم يوجد التمليك أيضاً فعل تقدير أن تكون الشفعة نفس ذلك التمليك كيف يتصور ثبوتها بعقد البيع واستقرارها بالإشهاد وأيضاً قد صرحوا بأن حكم الشفعة جواز الطلب وثبوت الملك بالقضاء أو بالتراضي فلو كان نفس التمليك لما صلح شيء من جواز طلب الشفعة وثبوت الملك بالقضاء أو بالتراضي لأن يكون حكماً للشفعة. أما الأول فلأنه لا شك أن المقصود من طلب الشفعة إنما هو الوصول إلى ملك المنفعة المشفوعة، وعند حصول تملكها الذي هو الشفعة على الفرض المذكور لا يبقى جواز طلب الشفعة ضرورة بطلان طلب الحاصل وحكم الشيء يقارنه أو يعقبه، فالأظهر عندي في تعريف الشفعة ما ذكره صاحب غاية البيان حيث قال : ثم الشفعة عبارة عن حق التملك في العقار لدفع ضرر الجوار اهـ. والجواب أن المراد بالوجوب والاستقرار استقرار حق الأخذ لا نفسه، وقولهم حكم الشفعة جواز الطلب يعين حكم حق الأخذ فلا إيراد.
Book of Pre-emption: Ownership of the plot compulsorily upon the purchaser for what he paid, and it is established for the partner in the same sold property, and it is established for the purchaser to take from the property. The appropriateness of placing shuf'a after ghasp is that in both a person owns another's property without his consent, and the right is to give precedence to it because it is legislated unlike ghasp, but the need to know ghasp is greater due to many related rulings so it was given precedence. Discussion of it has aspects: first its linguistic meaning, second its legal meaning, third explanation of its proof, fourth explanation of its cause, fifth its pillar, sixth its condition, seventh its ruling and description. Linguistically it is derived from shaf' which is the opposite of witr. Legally it is what the author mentioned. Its proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged shuf'a in every partnership not yet divided in its fourth or wall, and he said: The neighbor has more right to his neighbor's shuf'a. Its cause is to repel the harm that arises from bad neighboring continuously in terms of lighting fire, raising walls, and raising dust. Its pillar is the seller. Its condition is that the subject be real estate, upper or lower, owned for a price. Its ruling is the permissibility of demanding shuf'a when its cause is realized. Its description is that taking by it is like a new purchase so that what is established by purchase is established such as return by option of inspection and stipulation. He (the author) said: (It is ownership of the plot compulsorily upon the purchaser for what he paid) in law, and some added partnership or adjacency. So his saying 'ownership' is a genus including ownership of the substance and usufructs, his saying 'the plot' separates excluding ownership of usufructs. His saying 'compulsorily' separates excluding sale which is with consent. His saying 'for what he paid' means in reality or legally as will come in wine etc. The intended is ownership of the plot or part of it to include when one of the pre-emptors buys it. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: The neighbor bought a house and it had another neighbor from another side and he demanded shuf'a – the house is divided between the buyer and the neighbor in halves. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: It is only established in lands whose corpus is owned, so not established in lands that the Imam took for the treasury and given to people for sharecropping so they had buildings and trees in them; the sale of such lands is invalid. It is only established by right of ownership in lands, even if a house is sold belonging to a partner in the same sold property, then in the right of the sold property like water and path if specific, then for the neighbor adjacent to it; a waqf house – no shuf'a for the waqf and the administrator does not take it. Ibn Qadi Zadih said: If the reality of shuf'a is ownership, then it necessarily follows that his statement 'shuf'a is established by the sale contract and settled by testimony' is not valid because establishment is inconceivable without actual occurrence, and at the time of the sale contract and testimony, taking by mutual consent or by judge's decree has not occurred, nor has ownership occurred. So if we suppose that shuf'a is that very ownership, how can it be imagined that it is established by the sale contract and settled by testimony? Also they have stated that the ruling of shuf'a is permissibility of demand and establishment of ownership by judge's decree or mutual consent. So if it were the very ownership, then nothing of 'permissibility of demand' and 'establishment of ownership by judge's decree or mutual consent' would be suitable to be a ruling for shuf'a. As for the first, there is no doubt that the purpose of demanding shuf'a is to reach ownership of the pre-empted usufruct, and when its ownership is obtained, which is shuf'a on the supposed assumption, the permissibility of demanding shuf'a does not remain necessarily because of the invalidity of demanding something already obtained, and the ruling of a thing is concomitant or follows it. So the more apparent to me in the definition of shuf'a is what the author of Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned: 'Shuf'a is an expression for the right of ownership in real estate to repel harm of neighbor.' End. The answer: What is meant by obligation and settlement is the settlement of the right to take, not itself, and their saying 'the ruling of shuf'a is permissibility of demand' specifies the ruling of the right to take, so there is no objection.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage defines the Islamic legal concept of shuf'a (pre-emption). It opens by stating the legal definition: shuf'a is the compulsory acquisition of a sold property from the buyer at the price he paid. The commentator then explains the appropriateness of discussing shuf'a after ghasp (usurpation) — both involve taking another's property without consent, but shuf'a is legislated. Seven aspects of shuf'a are outlined: linguistic meaning (derived from shaf' meaning pair, opposite of odd), legal definition as given by the author, proof (hadith of the Prophet judging shuf'a for undivided partners and the hadith 'the neighbor is more entitled to his neighbor's shuf'a'), cause (preventing harm from bad neighbors), pillar (the seller), condition (the property must be real estate owned for a price), ruling (permissibility to demand), and description (taking by shuf'a is like a new purchase, with options of inspection and stipulation). The commentary then dissects the author's definition: 'ownership' is a genus including substance and usufructs; 'plot' excludes usufructs; 'compulsorily' excludes voluntary sale; 'for what he paid' means actual price or legally as in wine cases. An example from al-Tatarkhaniyya illustrates that if a neighbor buys a house, another neighbor can demand shuf'a and take half. Shuf'a applies only to land owned in fee simple, not to land held by the treasury and given for sharecropping. The passage then addresses an objection by Ibn Qadi Zadih: if shuf'a is defined as ownership, how can it be said to be established by sale and settled by testimony? The response explains that what is meant is the right to take ownership, not the act itself; the ruling of permissibility of demand pertains to that right. The definition from Ghayat al-Bayan—'shuf'a is the right of ownership in real estate to repel neighborly harm'—is preferred because it avoids the confusion. The passage concludes that there is no real objection.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): A right to compulsorily purchase a sold property from the buyer at the price he paid, to prevent harm from bad neighboring.
الشفع (al-shaf'): Linguistically, the pair or even number, opposite of odd (witr). Shuf'a is derived from it because it joins two shares together.
الجبر (al-jabr): Compulsion; shuf'a is compulsory on the buyer, unlike sale which is with consent.
الخليط (al-khalit): Partner in the property itself (sharikat al-milk).
حق الملك (haqq al-milk): Right of ownership; shuf'a is established by right of ownership in the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what is the cause (sabab) of shuf'a?
A) The buyer's consent
B) Partnership in the property
C) Repelling harm from bad neighboring
D) The seller's willingness

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a is a right to compulsory ownership of real estate to prevent neighborly harm, and its definition must be understood as the right to take, not the taking itself.

The Nature of Shuf'a: Right vs. Ownership
Addresses a logical objection to the definition and refines it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why defining shuf'a as ownership leads to logical contradiction and state the correct definition as a right to ownership.

Core Idea
Shuf'a is a right to compulsory ownership, not the act of ownership itself; its ‘establishment’ refers to the right becoming available.

The passage presents a sophisticated objection by Ibn Qadi Zadih: if shuf'a is defined as ownership (tamlik), then it cannot be 'established' by the sale contract before actual transfer. The Hanafi response refines the definition to solve this logical problem. This lesson clarifies the precise nature of shuf'a as a right (haqq) and shows how careful wording avoids inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Restate Ibn Qadi Zadih's objection
If shuf'a is ownership itself, then it cannot be 'established' by sale because ownership doesn't occur until the pre-emptor takes it. Also, the ruling of shuf'a (permissibility of demand) would be impossible if shuf'a already includes ownership.
Focus on the logical chain: definition → consequence → contradiction.
2
Identify the two parts of the objection
First part: establishment vs actual occurrence. Second part: permissibility of demand vs ownership already achieved.
These are two separate but related arguments.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
What is meant by 'obligation and settlement' is the settlement of the right to take (haqq al-akhdh), not the ownership itself. The ruling of permissibility of demand pertains to that right, not the completed ownership.
This solves both parts: the right is established by sale, and demand is to exercise it.
4
Note the preferred definition from Ghayat al-Bayan
The commentator prefers: 'Shuf'a is an expression for the right of ownership in real estate to repel harm of neighbor.' This explicitly uses 'right' (haqq) and avoids confusion.
This becomes the refined definition.

كتاب الشفعة تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه وتجب للخليط في نفس المبيع وتجب المشتري به الأخذ من مال. وجه مناسبة الشفعة بالغصب تملك الإنسان مال غيره بلا رضاه في كل منهما، والحق تقديمها عليه لكونها مشروعة دونه ولكن توفر الحاجة إلى معرفته لكثرة الأحكام المتعلقة أوجبت تقديمه والكلام فيها من وجوه الأول في معناه لغة، والثاني شرعاً، والثالث في بيان دليلها، والرابع في بيان سببها، والخامس في ركنها، والسادس في شرطها، والسابع في حكمها وصفتها، فهي لغة مأخوذة من الشفع الذي هو ضد الوتر، وشرعاً ما ذكره المؤلف، ودليلها ما روي أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قضى بالشفعة في كل شركة لم تقسم ربعه أو حائطه وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام الجار أحق بشفعة جاره وسببها دفع الضرر الذي ينشأ من سوء المجاورة على الدوام من حيث إيقاد النار وإعلاء الجدار وإثارة الغبار. وركنها هو أو من البائع. وشرطها كون المحل عقاراً علواً كان أو سفلاً مملوكاً ببدل هو وأما حكمها فهو جواز طلب الشفعة عند تحقق سببها. وصفتها أن الأخذ بها بمنزلة شراء مبتدأ حتى يثبت ما يثبت بالشراء نحو الرد بخيار الرؤية والشرط. قال رحمه الله : (هي تملك البقعة جبراً على المشتري بما قام عليه هذا في الشرع وزاد بعضهم شركة أو جوار. فقوله تمليك جنس شمل تمليك العين والمنافع، وقوله «البقعة» فصل أخرج به تمليك المنافع. وقوله «جبراً» أخرج به البيع فإنه يكون بالرضا، وقوله بما قام عليه» يعني حقيقة أو حكماً كما سيأتي في الخمر وغيره والمراد تمليك البقعة أو بعضها ليشمل ما إذا اشتراها أحد شفعائها ففي التتارخانية : اشترى الجار داراً ولها جار آخر من جانب آخر وطلب الشفعة تقسم الدار بين المشتري والجار نصفين. وفي التتارخانية وإنما تجب في الأراضي التي يملك رقابها حتى لا تجب في الأراضي التي حازها الإمام لبيت المال وتدفع للناس مزارعة فصار لهم فيها بناء وأشجار فإن بيع هذه الأراضي باطل، وإنما تجب بحق الملك في الأراضي حتى لو بيعت دار للخليط في نفس المبيع ثم في حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق إن كان خاصاً ثم للجار بجنبها دار الوقف فلا شفعة للوقف ولا يأخذها المتولي قال ابن قاضي زاده : إذا كان حقيقة الشفعة التمليك لزم أن لا يكون لقوله الشفعة تثبت بعقد البيع وتستقر بالإشهاد صحة إذ الثبوت لا يتصور بدون التحقق وحين عقد البيع والإشهاد لم يوجد الأخذ بالتراضي ولا بقضاء القاضي ولم يوجد التمليك أيضاً فعل تقدير أن تكون الشفعة نفس ذلك التمليك كيف يتصور ثبوتها بعقد البيع واستقرارها بالإشهاد وأيضاً قد صرحوا بأن حكم الشفعة جواز الطلب وثبوت الملك بالقضاء أو بالتراضي فلو كان نفس التمليك لما صلح شيء من جواز طلب الشفعة وثبوت الملك بالقضاء أو بالتراضي لأن يكون حكماً للشفعة. أما الأول فلأنه لا شك أن المقصود من طلب الشفعة إنما هو الوصول إلى ملك المنفعة المشفوعة، وعند حصول تملكها الذي هو الشفعة على الفرض المذكور لا يبقى جواز طلب الشفعة ضرورة بطلان طلب الحاصل وحكم الشيء يقارنه أو يعقبه، فالأظهر عندي في تعريف الشفعة ما ذكره صاحب غاية البيان حيث قال : ثم الشفعة عبارة عن حق التملك في العقار لدفع ضرر الجوار اهـ. والجواب أن المراد بالوجوب والاستقرار استقرار حق الأخذ لا نفسه، وقولهم حكم الشفعة جواز الطلب يعين حكم حق الأخذ فلا إيراد.
Book of Pre-emption: Ownership of the plot compulsorily upon the purchaser for what he paid, and it is established for the partner in the same sold property, and it is established for the purchaser to take from the property. The appropriateness of placing shuf'a after ghasp is that in both a person owns another's property without his consent, and the right is to give precedence to it because it is legislated unlike ghasp, but the need to know ghasp is greater due to many related rulings so it was given precedence. Discussion of it has aspects: first its linguistic meaning, second its legal meaning, third explanation of its proof, fourth explanation of its cause, fifth its pillar, sixth its condition, seventh its ruling and description. Linguistically it is derived from shaf' which is the opposite of witr. Legally it is what the author mentioned. Its proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged shuf'a in every partnership not yet divided in its fourth or wall, and he said: The neighbor has more right to his neighbor's shuf'a. Its cause is to repel the harm that arises from bad neighboring continuously in terms of lighting fire, raising walls, and raising dust. Its pillar is the seller. Its condition is that the subject be real estate, upper or lower, owned for a price. Its ruling is the permissibility of demanding shuf'a when its cause is realized. Its description is that taking by it is like a new purchase so that what is established by purchase is established such as return by option of inspection and stipulation. He (the author) said: (It is ownership of the plot compulsorily upon the purchaser for what he paid) in law, and some added partnership or adjacency. So his saying 'ownership' is a genus including ownership of the substance and usufructs, his saying 'the plot' separates excluding ownership of usufructs. His saying 'compulsorily' separates excluding sale which is with consent. His saying 'for what he paid' means in reality or legally as will come in wine etc. The intended is ownership of the plot or part of it to include when one of the pre-emptors buys it. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: The neighbor bought a house and it had another neighbor from another side and he demanded shuf'a – the house is divided between the buyer and the neighbor in halves. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: It is only established in lands whose corpus is owned, so not established in lands that the Imam took for the treasury and given to people for sharecropping so they had buildings and trees in them; the sale of such lands is invalid. It is only established by right of ownership in lands, even if a house is sold belonging to a partner in the same sold property, then in the right of the sold property like water and path if specific, then for the neighbor adjacent to it; a waqf house – no shuf'a for the waqf and the administrator does not take it. Ibn Qadi Zadih said: If the reality of shuf'a is ownership, then it necessarily follows that his statement 'shuf'a is established by the sale contract and settled by testimony' is not valid because establishment is inconceivable without actual occurrence, and at the time of the sale contract and testimony, taking by mutual consent or by judge's decree has not occurred, nor has ownership occurred. So if we suppose that shuf'a is that very ownership, how can it be imagined that it is established by the sale contract and settled by testimony? Also they have stated that the ruling of shuf'a is permissibility of demand and establishment of ownership by judge's decree or mutual consent. So if it were the very ownership, then nothing of 'permissibility of demand' and 'establishment of ownership by judge's decree or mutual consent' would be suitable to be a ruling for shuf'a. As for the first, there is no doubt that the purpose of demanding shuf'a is to reach ownership of the pre-empted usufruct, and when its ownership is obtained, which is shuf'a on the supposed assumption, the permissibility of demanding shuf'a does not remain necessarily because of the invalidity of demanding something already obtained, and the ruling of a thing is concomitant or follows it. So the more apparent to me in the definition of shuf'a is what the author of Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned: 'Shuf'a is an expression for the right of ownership in real estate to repel harm of neighbor.' End. The answer: What is meant by obligation and settlement is the settlement of the right to take, not itself, and their saying 'the ruling of shuf'a is permissibility of demand' specifies the ruling of the right to take, so there is no objection.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage defines the Islamic legal concept of shuf'a (pre-emption). It opens by stating the legal definition: shuf'a is the compulsory acquisition of a sold property from the buyer at the price he paid. The commentator then explains the appropriateness of discussing shuf'a after ghasp (usurpation) — both involve taking another's property without consent, but shuf'a is legislated. Seven aspects of shuf'a are outlined: linguistic meaning (derived from shaf' meaning pair, opposite of odd), legal definition as given by the author, proof (hadith of the Prophet judging shuf'a for undivided partners and the hadith 'the neighbor is more entitled to his neighbor's shuf'a'), cause (preventing harm from bad neighbors), pillar (the seller), condition (the property must be real estate owned for a price), ruling (permissibility to demand), and description (taking by shuf'a is like a new purchase, with options of inspection and stipulation). The commentary then dissects the author's definition: 'ownership' is a genus including substance and usufructs; 'plot' excludes usufructs; 'compulsorily' excludes voluntary sale; 'for what he paid' means actual price or legally as in wine cases. An example from al-Tatarkhaniyya illustrates that if a neighbor buys a house, another neighbor can demand shuf'a and take half. Shuf'a applies only to land owned in fee simple, not to land held by the treasury and given for sharecropping. The passage then addresses an objection by Ibn Qadi Zadih: if shuf'a is defined as ownership, how can it be said to be established by sale and settled by testimony? The response explains that what is meant is the right to take ownership, not the act itself; the ruling of permissibility of demand pertains to that right. The definition from Ghayat al-Bayan—'shuf'a is the right of ownership in real estate to repel neighborly harm'—is preferred because it avoids the confusion. The passage concludes that there is no real objection.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): A right to compulsorily purchase a sold property from the buyer at the price he paid, to prevent harm from bad neighboring.
الحق (al-haqq): A legal right or entitlement. In shuf'a, it is the right to demand ownership, not the ownership itself.
التمليك (al-tamlik): The act of making someone owner; ownership transfer.
حق الأخذ (haqq al-akhdh): The right to take; this is what is actually established by the sale contract in shuf'a.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi response say is actually 'established' (thabita) by the sale contract in shuf'a?
A) Ownership of the property for the pre-emptor
B) The right to take ownership (haqq al-akhdh)
C) The buyer's right to resist
D) The price to be paid

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a is a right to ownership, not the ownership itself; its establishment refers to the right becoming available, and this distinction solves the logical problem in the definition.

The Hierarchy of Shuf'a Claimants
Establishes who is entitled to shuf'a and in what order, with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of entitlement to shuf'a, identify the hadith proofs for partners and neighbors, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i restriction argument.

Core Idea
Shuf'a belongs first to the partner in property, then partner in rights, then adjacent neighbor — harm severity determines priority.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'iq clarifies the hierarchy of persons entitled to shuf'a (pre-emption). You will see how the Hanafi school uses two hadiths to include the neighbor, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to partners only. The underlying principle is repelling continuous harm: the more connected the party, the stronger their right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of claimants
The matn states shuf'a is established for (1) the partner in the property itself, (2) the partner in rights like water/way if specific, and (3) the adjacent neighbor. Write down these three in order.
The partner in rights must have a specific (khass) right, not a public one.
2
Locate the primary hadith for partners
The text cites: 'قضى بالشفعة في كل شركة لم تقسم'. Identify that this hadith is the core evidence for the partner's right. Note its wording: 'in every undivided partnership'.
This hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
The objection: the definite article in 'al-shuf'a' implies restriction (qasr) to partners only, excluding neighbors. Trace how the objector argues that 'al' is for genus and implies the negative, so shuf'a is only for partners.
This is a linguistic argument about the scope of the text.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The commentator answers that another hadith explicitly gives the neighbor the right: 'الجار أحق بشفعة جاره'. Therefore, the restriction in the first hadith is not absolute. Write down both hadiths and see how they complement each other.
The Hanafis hold that the second hadith qualifies the first, not abrogates it.
5
Apply the ranking rationale
The order is based on 'دفع الضرر الدائم' – repelling continuous harm. The partner in property suffers the most harm, so gets the strongest right; then partner in rights (less strong); then the neighbor. Recognize that the weaker can only claim after the stronger waives.
This principle explains why shuf'a is a right, not a duty, and why priorities are fixed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وتجب للخليط في نفس المبيع يعني تثبت للشريك في نفس المبيع . أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قضى بالشفعة في كل الشركة لم تقسم ربعه، واعترض بأن روي الحديث وإن دل على بعض المدعي وهو ثبوت حق الشفعة للشريك الآخر إلا أنه يبقى بعضه الآخر وهو ثبوتها لغير الشريك أيضاً كالجار الملاصق لأن اللام في الشفعة المذكورة للجنس لعدم العهد، وتعريف المسند إليه بلام الجنس يفيد قصر المسند إليه على المسند فاقتضى انتفاء غير الشريك كالجار والجواب أن ثبوت حق الشفعة للجار أفاده حديث آخر حق الشفعة من فظهر أن القصر غير حقيقي. قال رحمه الله : ( وتجب للخليط في نفس المبيع ثم في حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق إن كان خاصاً ثم للجار الملاصق يعني يثبت بعد الأول للشريك في حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق؛ أما الطريق فقد تقدم دليله، وأما الجار فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الجار أحق بشفعة جاره وإنما وجبت مرتبة على الترتيب الذي ذكره هنا لأنها وجبت لدفع الضرر الدائم الذي يلحقه، وكل ما كان أكثر اتصالاً كأن أخص ضرراً وأشد فكان أحق بها لقوة الموجب لها فليس للأضعف أن يأخذه مع وجود الأقوى إلا إذا ترك فله أن يأخذ إن شهد. وقال الشافعي : لا تجب للجار. وقوله إن كان خاصاً يعني الشرب والطريق وإن لم يكن خاصاً لا الشفعة والطريق الخاص أن يكون غير نافذ وإن كان نافذاً فليس بخاص، وإن يستحق به كانت سكة غير نافذة يتشعب منها سكة غير نافذة فبيعت دار في السفلى فلأهلها الشفعة لا
He (the author) said: And it is established for the partner in the same sold property, i.e., it is proved for the partner in the same sold property. That the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged shuf'a in every partnership not divided in its fourth. An objection is made that the hadith, although it indicates part of what is claimed, which is the establishment of the right of shuf'a for the other partner, yet the other part remains, which is its establishment for other than the partner as well, such as the adjacent neighbor, because the definite article in 'al-shuf'a' mentioned is for the genus due to lack of prior reference, and defining the subject with the definite article of genus implies restriction of the subject to the predicate, so it necessitates negation of other than the partner like the neighbor. The answer is that the establishment of the right of shuf'a for the neighbor is indicated by another hadith: the neighbor has more right to his neighbor's shuf'a. So it becomes clear that the restriction is not real. He (the author) said: And it is established for the partner in the same sold property, then in the right of the sold property like water and path if specific, then for the adjacent neighbor, i.e., it is proved after the first for the partner in the right of the sold property like water and path. As for the path, its proof has already come. As for the neighbor, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The neighbor is more entitled to his neighbor's shuf'a.' And it is established in the order mentioned here because it is established to repel the continuous harm that afflicts him, and whatever is more connected (such that harm is more specific and severe) is more entitled to it due to the strength of the cause. So the weaker one cannot take it in the presence of the stronger, unless the stronger leaves it, then the weaker may take if he bears witness. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not established for the neighbor. And his saying 'if specific' means the water and path; and if not specific, then no shuf'a. The specific path is that it is not through; if it is through then it is not specific. And if it is a dead-end alley branching from another dead-end alley, and a house at the lower end is sold, then its inhabitants have shuf'a, not...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage explains who is entitled to shuf'a and the priority among them. The author's matn states that shuf'a is established first for the partner in the same sold property (khalit fi nafs al-mabi'), then for the partner in the rights of the sold property like water and path (if they are specific), and then for the adjacent neighbor (jar mulasiq). The commentator provides the proof from the hadith: the Prophet judged shuf'a in every undivided partnership. An objection is raised: the hadith uses the definite article 'al' in 'al-shuf'a', which implies restriction (qasr) to partners only, excluding neighbors. The answer is that another hadith shows the neighbor's right: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his neighbor's shuf'a.' So the restriction in the first hadith is not absolute. The priority order is based on the intensity of harm: the partner in the property has the strongest connection and thus the strongest right; then the partner in rights; then the neighbor. The weaker cannot claim while the stronger is present, but if the stronger waives the right, the weaker may take, provided he gives testimony (i.e., demands properly). The passage then notes the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i does not grant shuf'a to the neighbor at all. The condition of the path being 'specific' is then explained: it must be a non-through path (dead-end); if it is a public thoroughfare, it is not specific and thus no shuf'a in it. An example is given: if there is a dead-end alley branching from another dead-end alley, and a house at the lower end is sold, the residents of that alley have shuf'a. The passage ends abruptly.

Key Terms
الخليط في نفس المبيع (al-khalit fi nafs al-mabi'): The co-owner (partner) in the specific property that was sold.
حق المبيع (haqq al-mabi'): Rights attached to the sold property, such as a right of way (sharb) or path (tariq) that are exclusive (specific) to the property.
الجار الملاصق (al-jar al-mulasiq): The adjacent neighbor whose property directly adjoins the sold property.
الطريق الخاص (al-tariq al-khass): A non-through path (dead-end) that is not a public thoroughfare.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in what order are the following entitled to shuf'a?
A) Adjacent neighbor, partner in the property, partner in rights
B) Partner in the property, partner in rights, adjacent neighbor
C) Partner in rights, adjacent neighbor, partner in the property
D) Adjacent neighbor, partner in rights, partner in the property

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a right in Hanafi fiqh follows a fixed three-tier order: partner in the property, then partner in specific rights, then adjacent neighbor — all based on the degree of potential harm.
